<span id="freeTextContainer6452635901862578723">Andromeda Strain is a classic. Of course Congo, Rising Sun, and Jurassic Park are his 'biggies'. For me, I think his creativity was most unique in Timeline. The book was absolutely outstanding for me. it involves time &amp; place travel, and manages to handle some of the paradoxes thereto quite well.<br /><br />THE MOVIE WAS A HORRIBLE RECOUNTING OF THIS STORY !!! The movie was made at a time when FINALLY technology in film making was such that it might possibly be able to do this story justice. And then th</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6452635901862578723">Andromeda Strain is a classic. Of course Congo, Rising Sun, and Jurassic Park are his 'biggies'. For me, I think his creativity was most unique in Timeline. The book was absolutely outstanding for me. it involves time &amp; place travel, and manages to handle some of the paradoxes thereto quite well.<br /><br />THE MOVIE WAS A HORRIBLE RECOUNTING OF THIS STORY !!! The movie was made at a time when FINALLY technology in film making was such that it might possibly be able to do this story justice. And then the producers cheaped out and did an almost no-tech film, left out huge events and had to change others to patch up the horrible mess they made. It was caste wrong. I want that money back, almost as much as the cabbage I threw down for Johnny Pneumonic (aka worst modern film).<br /><br />Movie - heck no. Book - ohh yeaaahh. I don't usually get all caught up in differences between books and their movies as there's literally amost no way to do any good book justice in less than 4-6 hours of film, but in this case I'm simply emparting friendly advice.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16814690364484393141">I recently read <a title="Doomsday Book (Oxford Time Travel, #1) by Connie Willis" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24983.Doomsday_Book__Oxford_Time_Travel___1_">Doomsday Book</a> by Connie Willis. Timeline shares themes with it. Historians travel through time to the middle ages, including 1348, the year of the Black Death. The circumstances are quite different, though. In Timeline, the corporation that developed the time travel technology had in mind cashing in on it, just as in Crichton's Jurassic Park. And back in medieval times, things are quite different between the two books. In Timeline, our time travelers get mixed up in aristocratic</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16814690364484393141">I recently read <a title="Doomsday Book (Oxford Time Travel, #1) by Connie Willis" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24983.Doomsday_Book__Oxford_Time_Travel___1_">Doomsday Book</a> by Connie Willis. Timeline shares themes with it. Historians travel through time to the middle ages, including 1348, the year of the Black Death. The circumstances are quite different, though. In Timeline, the corporation that developed the time travel technology had in mind cashing in on it, just as in Crichton's Jurassic Park. And back in medieval times, things are quite different between the two books. In Timeline, our time travelers get mixed up in aristocratic intrigue and warring fiefdoms. In both, they were rescued just in the nick of time.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1117361219">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1117361219" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/8778774-aura" class="left imgcol" title="Aura"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1439291614p2/8778774.jpg" alt="Aura" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1117361219?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 11, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/8778774-aura" class="user" title="Aura">Aura</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7669.Timeline" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780099244721" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1117361219">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11724832028099128125">Have you read <a title="Jurassic Park by Michael Crichton" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6424171.Jurassic_Park">Jurassic Park</a>? No? But you must have seen the movie. <br /><br /><a title="Timeline by Michael Crichton" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7669.Timeline">Timeline</a> is a science fiction novel about time travel first published in 1999, written by <a title="Michael Crichton" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5194.Michael_Crichton">Michael Crichton</a>, the creator of <a title="Jurassic Park by Michael Crichton" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6424171.Jurassic_Park">Jurassic Park</a> and <a title="The Lost World (Jurassic Park, #2) by Michael Crichton" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8650.The_Lost_World__Jurassic_Park___2_">The Lost World</a>.<br /><br />The novel is narrated in the third person and follows multiple Points of View. The most notable characters are André Marek, Chris Hughes, and Kate Erickson, three grad students working on an archaeological dig in France. The three of them are sent back in time by the corporati</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11724832028099128125">Have you read <a title="Jurassic Park by Michael Crichton" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6424171.Jurassic_Park">Jurassic Park</a>? No? But you must have seen the movie. <br /><br /><a title="Timeline by Michael Crichton" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7669.Timeline">Timeline</a> is a science fiction novel about time travel first published in 1999, written by <a title="Michael Crichton" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5194.Michael_Crichton">Michael Crichton</a>, the creator of <a title="Jurassic Park by Michael Crichton" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6424171.Jurassic_Park">Jurassic Park</a> and <a title="The Lost World (Jurassic Park, #2) by Michael Crichton" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8650.The_Lost_World__Jurassic_Park___2_">The Lost World</a>.<br /><br />The novel is narrated in the third person and follows multiple Points of View. The most notable characters are André Marek, Chris Hughes, and Kate Erickson, three grad students working on an archaeological dig in France. The three of them are sent back in time by the corporation that employs them, when their professor vanishes after taking the same temporal trip. <br /><br />The first thing that the book establishes about time travel? <br /><strong>
  <em>“The very concept of time travel makes no sense, since time doesn’t flow. The fact that we think time passes is just an accident of our nervous systems — of the way things look to us. In reality, time doesn’t pass; we pass. Time itself is invariant. It just is. Therefore, past and future aren’t separate locations, the way New York and Paris are separate locations. And since the past isn’t a location, you can’t travel to it.”</em>
</strong><br /><br />It's not possible. You can't go back in time. Time travel is pure fantasy, not science fiction.<br />So what strategy the author used for the characters to visit the Earth during an earlier time period? The multiverse theory and quantum computing:<br /><br /><strong>
  <em>“Let me explain what David is talking about,” Gordon said to the others. “Ordinary computers make calculations using two electron states, which are designated one and zero. That’s how all computers work, by pushing around ones and zeros. But twenty years ago, Richard Feynman suggested it might be possible to make an extremely powerful computer using all thirty-two quantum states of an electron. Many laboratories are now trying to build these quantum computers. Their advantage is unimaginably great power — so great that you can indeed describe and compress a three-dimensional living object into an electron stream. Exactly like a fax. You can then transmit the electron stream through a quantum foam wormhole and reconstruct it in another universe. And that’s what we do. It’s not quantum teleportation. It’s not particle entanglement. It’s direct transmission to another universe.”</em>
</strong><br /><br />I think it's a pretty good explanation. And if you're the kind of reader bored by theories and science, there's so much action, adventure, and danger on these pages, almost enough to rival that of <a title="Jurassic Park by Michael Crichton" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6424171.Jurassic_Park">Jurassic Park</a>.<br /><br />An afterword the author wrote in the acknowledgements section:<br /><strong>
  <em>"A word about time travel. While it is true that quantum teleportation has been demonstrated in laboratories around the world, the practical application of such phenomena lies in the future. The ideas presented in this book were stimulated by the speculations of David Deutsch, Kip Thorne, Paul Nahin and Charles Bennett, among others. What appears here may amuse them, but they would not take it seriously. This is a novel: time travel rests firmly in the realm of fantasy."</em>
</strong></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11724832028099128125">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_35741423">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/35741423" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1579663-elyse" class="left imgcol" title="Elyse"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1367477965p2/1579663.jpg" alt="Elyse" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/35741423?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 19, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1579663-elyse" class="user" title="Elyse">Elyse</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Those interested in time travel and medieval history</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Elyse by: </span>
      My friend
  </div>



    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer35741423">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12801383552929354362">Professor Johnston is leading an excavation trip in France with several of his students, but he leaves to speak with the founder of the company that's sponsoring the dig. There he finds out that the company has built a time machine that can transport you to 14th century France. He decides to see for himself what life was really like back there. But he is trapped and leaves clues for his students to find in the future, informing them that he is lost in the past. From there, they must travel back</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12801383552929354362">Professor Johnston is leading an excavation trip in France with several of his students, but he leaves to speak with the founder of the company that's sponsoring the dig. There he finds out that the company has built a time machine that can transport you to 14th century France. He decides to see for himself what life was really like back there. But he is trapped and leaves clues for his students to find in the future, informing them that he is lost in the past. From there, they must travel back to rescue him, immersing themselves in the very history they are studying.<br /><br />My friend was a huge fan of Michael Crichton and one of her favorite books was Timeline. She recommended it to me but before I got the chance to read it, she dragged me off to see the movie. I was impressed by the movie and decided I would read the book. However, I wasn't quite as impressed by the book. That's not to say that I didn't like the book. I did enjoy it. It was just very difficult for me to understand. There are a lot of scientific terms and descriptions that I, personally, had trouble understanding.<br /><br />Other than that, the story was very interesting and, after reading it, I was less impressed by the movie the second time I saw it. As always, the book is better than the movie.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12801383552929354362">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_537027225">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/537027225" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4665768-alyssa-archambo" class="left imgcol" title="Alyssa Archambo"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1397027844p2/4665768.jpg" alt="Alyssa Archambo" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/537027225?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 02, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4665768-alyssa-archambo" class="user" title="Alyssa Archambo">Alyssa Archambo</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/701996.Timeline" title="Audio CD 9780375404368" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4665768-alyssa-archambo?shelf=science-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4665768-alyssa-archambo?shelf=historical-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4665768-alyssa-archambo?shelf=thriller" class="actionLinkLite">thriller</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4665768-alyssa-archambo?shelf=adventure" class="actionLinkLite">adventure</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4665768-alyssa-archambo?shelf=time-travel" class="actionLinkLite">time-travel</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer537027225">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10514679722490044244">Many might be familiar with Timeline from the movie adaptation with Paul Walker and Gerard Butler -- I saw that movie ages ago when it came out and finally got around to reading the book. I can't really compare it to the movie, because I saw that so long ago, but I thoroughly enjoyed the book. Timeline is about a group of archaeologists who must travel to the fourteenth century (during a time of war) to rescue their professor.<br /><br />Honestly, I was surprised by how much I enjoyed this book. Though I lo</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10514679722490044244">Many might be familiar with Timeline from the movie adaptation with Paul Walker and Gerard Butler -- I saw that movie ages ago when it came out and finally got around to reading the book. I can't really compare it to the movie, because I saw that so long ago, but I thoroughly enjoyed the book. Timeline is about a group of archaeologists who must travel to the fourteenth century (during a time of war) to rescue their professor.<br /><br />Honestly, I was surprised by how much I enjoyed this book. Though I love audiobooks, I'm always wary of committing myself to anything over seven or eight hours, because listening to the same voice for longer than that can get tedious. Thankfully, John Bedford Lloyd is a brilliant narrator and really brought life to the characters and the story. In fact, I enjoyed spending the extra time with this novel and being able to immerse myself in its world.<br /><br />Anybody who likes an adventure story would probably like Timeline. My favorite part about it is that it has a nice mix of historical fiction, mystery/thriller, and science fiction. There's something for everyone, and I love reading a story that is able to successfully bring together a variety of genres. Although, I have to say, some of the science fiction explanation was a little too detailed, making it confusing and leaving quite a few plot holes. It would have been better without the attempt to explain the time travel scientifically, I think. But putting that aside, Crichton has created a solidly entertaining story.<br /><br />There's action, adventure, romance, intrigue, etc. Like I said before, there's something for everyone. It's told from multiple viewpoints, but at no point was I confused or lost. If you enjoy audiobooks, don't let the length scare you -- I had a great time listening to it. However, if you're not an audiobook fan, I think that reading it would be just as satisfying.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10514679722490044244">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('hMczLj1itBBD2ubvbpDuQZTKrmVsP3XfxAOdMhVIeEThEwz9z7Cg6s8CklQQ8Qjz3T1tfCXiMnWuCpig2d2OAQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

But when he arrives, Crane learns that the real trouble lies far below—on “Deep Storm,” a stunningly advanced science research facility built two miles beneath the surface on the ocean floor. The top secret structure has been designed for one purpose: to excavate a recently discovered undersea site that may hold the answers to a mystery steeped in centuries of myth and speculation.\n\nSworn to secrecy, Dr. Crane descends to Deep Storm. A year earlier, he is told, routine drilling uncovered the remains of mankind’s most sophisticated ancient civilization: the legendary Atlantis. But now that the site is being excavated, a series of disturbing illnesses has begun to affect the operation. Scientists and technicians are experiencing a bizarre array of symptoms—from simple fatigue to violent psychotic episodes. As Crane is indoctrinated into the strange world of Deep Storm and commences his investigation, he begins to suspect that the covert facility conceals something more complicated than a medical mystery.The discovery of Atlantis might, in fact, be a cover for something far more sinister . . . and deadly.\n\nLike Lincoln Child’s spectacular bestsellers coauthored with Douglas Preston (The Book of the Dead, Relic), Deep Storm melds scientific detail and gripping adventure in a superbly imagined, chillingly real journey into unknown territory.     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/5194.Michael_Crichton">About Michael Crichton</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/5194.Michael_Crichton"><img alt="5194" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1359042651p2/5194.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer1364102605366029070">Michael Crichton (1942–2008) was one of the most successful novelists of his generation, admired for his meticulous scientific research and fast-paced narrative. He graduated summa cum laude and earned his MD from Harvard Medical School in 1969. His first novel, <a title="Odds On" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18078737.Odds_On">Odds On</a> (1966), was written under the pseudonym <a title="John Lange" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/12619.John_Lange">John Lange</a> and was followed by seven more Lange novels. He also wrote as <a title="Michael Douglas" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/85503.Michael_Douglas">Michael Douglas</a></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1364102605366029070">Michael Crichton (1942–2008) was one of the most successful novelists of his generation, admired for his meticulous scientific research and fast-paced narrative. He graduated summa cum laude and earned his MD from Harvard Medical School in 1969. His first novel, <a title="Odds On" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18078737.Odds_On">Odds On</a> (1966), was written under the pseudonym <a title="John Lange" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/12619.John_Lange">John Lange</a> and was followed by seven more Lange novels. He also wrote as <a title="Michael Douglas" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/85503.Michael_Douglas">Michael Douglas</a> and <a title="Jeffery Hudson" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/607284.Jeffery_Hudson">Jeffery Hudson</a>. His novel <a title="A Case of Need" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=A%20Case%20of%20Need">A Case of Need</a> won the Edgar Award in 1969. Popular throughout the world, he has sold more than 200 million books. His novels have been translated into thirty-eight languages, and thirteen have been made into films.<br /><br />Michael Crichton passed away from lymphoma in 2008. He was 66 years old.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1364102605366029070">...more</a>

    </div>
